Jamison Brereton

29 (263)
Agni
Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra G─Бthina
16 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh, except anuс╣гс╣нubh 1, 4, 10, 12; jagat─л 6, 11, 14тАУ15
This hymn was composed to accompany the creation of a new fire for the sacrifice. This fire was created through friction using a fire drill that consisted of two pieces of wood. The upper fire-churning stick was held vertically, with one end in a recessed area in the lower piece of wood, which was horizontal. Wood chips were placed around the recessed area on the lower plank. The upper stick was then rotated back and forth, like a churn. In the later ritual this is done by wrapping a rope around the upper stick and pulling on one side and then the other to make the stick rotate back and forth. Eventually, enough heat was generated so that the wood chips caught fire.
This process of churning out the fire was regularly identified in the R╠еgvedic hymns with sexual intercourse, and this repeated image presents the upper fire-churning stick as the father, with phallic overtones especially in verse 1, and the lower fire-churning stick as the mother of fire. Another theme that runs throughout the hymn, and again a common one in Agni hymns, is the idea that Agni is born as a priest of the sacrifice, who carries the oblations (vss. 4, 7) and offers the sacrifice (vs. 8) and who is a sage poet (vss. 5, 12) and a Hotar (vss. 8, 16) in the company of the seven Hotars (vs. 14), the seven priests of the rite. The priests kindling Agni are named in verse 15: they are the Ku┼Ыikas, whose knowledge and ability to formulate the truth about Agni the hymn accentuates.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThis, the apparatus of attrition is ready; the genitive ration (of the flame) is ready; take up this (stick) the protectress of mankind, and let us churn the fire as has been done of old.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The apparatus of attrition is ready: ast─лdam adhimanthanam = asti prajananam kс╣Ыtam: adhimanthana is the stick, the string and the like plural ced upon the two pieces of wood to assist in their attrition;

Prajananam = begetting; may also connote a tuft of dry grass used to catch and carry the flame

Jamison Brereton

Here is the base for fire-churning; here is the readied begetting tool [=upper fire-churning stick].
Bring here the clanlordтАЩs lady [=lower fire-churning stick]. Let us churn Agni in the ancient way.

Griffith

HERE is the gear for friction, here tinder made ready for the spark.
Bring thou the Matron: we will rub Agni in ancient fashion forth.

Oldenberg

1 This is the support on which the rubbing (for producing the fire) is performed 2; the creative organ 3 has been prepared. Bring hither the house-wife 4; let us produce Agni by rubbing in the old way.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рдиреН ! рдпрджреАрджрдордзрд┐рдордиреНрдердирдорд╕реНрддрд┐ рдпрдЪреНрдЪ рдкреНрд░рдЬрдирдирдВ рдХреГрддрдорд╕реНрддрд┐ рддрд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдореЗрддрд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрдкрддреНрдиреАрдВ рд╡рдпрдВ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдерд╛рд╜рдЧреНрдирд┐рдВ рдордиреНрдерд╛рдореЗрд╡рд╛рд╜рд╜рднрд░ реерезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЕрде рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрджрдЧреНрдирд┐рд╡рд╛рдпреБрднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕рдГ рдХрд┐рдВ рдХрд┐рдВ рд╕рд╛рдзрдпрдиреНрддреАрддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ред

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЕрд╕реНрддрд┐) (рдЗрджрдореН) (рдЕрдзрд┐рдордиреНрдердирдореН) рдЙрдкрд░рд┐рд╕реНрдердВ рдордиреНрдердирдореН (рдЕрд╕реНрддрд┐) (рдкреНрд░рдЬрдирдирдореН) рдкреНрд░рдХрдЯрдирдореН (рдХреГрддрдореН) (рдПрддрд╛рдореН) (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрдкрддреНрдиреАрдореН) рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдпрд╛рдГ рдкрд╛рд▓рд┐рдХрд╛рдореН (рдЖ) (рднрд░) рд╕рдордиреНрддрд╛рджреНрдзрд░ (рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдореН) (рдордиреНрдерд╛рдо) (рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдерд╛) рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реИрд░рд┐рд╡ реерезрее

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпреЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ рдЙрдкрд░реНрдпреНрдпрдзрд╕реНрдерд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рдордиреНрдердирд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рд╕рдЩреНрдШрд░реНрд╖рдгреЗрди рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрддрдордЧреНрдирд┐рдВ рдЬрдирдпреЗрдпреБрд╕реНрддреЗ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрд╛рд▓рд┐рдХрд╛рдВ рд╢рдХреНрддрд┐рдВ рд▓рднрдиреНрддреЗ рдпрдерд╛ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реИрдГ рд╢рд┐рд▓реНрдкрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрдпрд╛рд╜рдЧреНрдиреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рд╕рдВрдкрд╛рджрд┐рддрд╛ рднрд╡реЗрддреНрддреЗрдиреИрд╡ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░реЗрдг рд╕рд░реНрд╡ рдЗрдорд╛рдВ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧреГрд╣реНрдгреАрдпреБрдГ реерезрее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

English translation:

тАЬJ─Бtavedas has been deposited in the two sticks as the embryo is deposited in pregnant women; Agni is to be adored day by day by vigilant men laden with oblations.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

As J─Бtavedas, who is placed within the two fire-churning sticks, like an unborn child well placed within women with child,
Agni is to be summoned day after day by those awake, by the sons of Manu bearing offerings.

Griffith

1n the two fire-sticks Jatavedas lieth, even as the well-set germ in pregnant women,
Agni who day by day must be exalted by men who watch and worship with oblations.

Oldenberg

In the two fire-sticks dwells G├вtavedas, as the germ (lies) safe in pregnant womenтАФAgni who should be magnified 1 day by day by wakeful men who bring offerings.

English translation:

тАЬAgni who is J─Бtavedas, we plural ce you upon the earth in the centre, in the plural ce of Iс╕╖─Б, for the purpose of receiving the oblation.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Yajus. 34.14-15; in the plural ce of iс╕╖─Б: iс╕╖─Бy─Бspade n─Бbh─Б pс╣Ыthivy─Бс╕е adhi, i.e. in the middle of the northern altar; the hymn is also cited in Aitareya Br─Бhmaс╣Зa 1.5

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen they rub (the sticks) with their arms the radiant Agni bursts forth from the wood like a fleet courser, and like the many-coloured car of the A┼Ыvins unresisted in its course, Agni spreads wide around consuming stones and trees.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

When they churn him with their arms, he shines out, like a prizewinning horse, flame-red here in the wood.
Unstoppable, like the shimmering (chariot) of the A┼Ыvins on its course [=the sun?], he avoids the stones, burning the grasses.

Griffith

When with their arms they rub him straight he shineth forth like a strong courser, red in colour, in the wood.
Bright, checkless, as it were upon the Atvins’ path, lie passeth by the stones and burneth up the grass.

Oldenberg

When they produce him by rubbing with their arms, he shines forth laming in the wood like a red race-horse. Like the bright one on the path of the Asvins 1 the unrestrained (Agni) spares the stones, burning the grass 2.

Geldner

Wenn sie mit den Armen ihn ausreiben, so erstrahlt er in den H├╢lzern r├╢tlich wie der Preisrenner. Unaufhaltsam wie der pr├дchtige Wagen der Asvin auf der Fahrt, verschont er die Steine, das Gras verbrennend.

Grassmann

Wenn sie mit den Armen reiben, so ergl├дnzt er hell in den H├╢lzern, wie ein rasches, lichtrothes Ross, wie ein gl├дnzendes, nicht zur├╝ckgehaltenes auf der Fahrt der Agvinen umgeht er die Steine [des Heerdes oder Feuerplatzcs], das Gras verbrennend.

Elizarenkova

рдЬрд╛рддрдГ рдордиреНрдердирд╛рдирдиреНрддрд░рдореБрддреНрдкрдиреНрдирдГ рд╕ рдЪ рдЪреЗрдХрд┐рддрд╛рдирдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдВ рдЬрд╛рдирд╛рдирдГ рд╕рдиреН рд╡рд╛рдЬреА рд╕рддрддрдЧрдордирд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡рдГ рд╡рд┐рдкреНрд░рдГ рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рднрд┐рдЬреНрдЮрдГ рдЕрдд рдПрд╡ рдХрд╡рд┐рд╢рд╕реНрддрдГ рдХрд╡рд┐рднрд┐рд░реНрдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡рд┐рднрд┐рд░реНрд╣реЛрддреГрднрд┐рдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддрдГ рд╕реБрджрд╛рдиреБрдГ рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБ рдХрд░реНрдордлрд▓рд╕реНрдп рджрд╛рддрд╛ рдПрд╡рдВрд╡рд┐рдзрдГ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рд░реЛрдЪрддреЗ рджреАрдкреНрдпрддреЗ ред рджреЗрд╡рд╛рд╕рдГ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рджрдпрдГ рдИрдбреНрдпрдВ рд╣реЛрддреНрд░рд╛рджрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддреНрдпрдВ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╡рд┐рджрдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рдЬрдЧрддреЛ рд╡реЗрджрд┐рддрд╛рд░рдВ рдпрдореН рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдореН рдЕрдзреНрд╡рд░реЗрд╖реБ рдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐рд╖реНрдЯреЛрдорд╛рджрд┐рдпрдЬреНрдЮреЗрд╖реБ рд╣рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╛рд╣рдВ рд╣рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╡реЛрдврд╛рд░рдореН рдЕрджрдзреБрдГ рд╡реНрдпрджрдзреБрдГ рд╕реЛрд╜рдЧреНрдирд┐рд░реНрджреАрдкреНрдпрддреЗ рдЗрддрд┐ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реЗрдгрд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ рее рдЪреЗрдХрд┐рддрд╛рдирдГ ред тАШ рдХрд┐рдд рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдиреЗ’ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рдпрдЩреНрд▓реБрдХрд┐ ’ рдЧреБрдгреЛ рдпрдЩреНрд▓реБрдХреЛрдГ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЕрднреНрдпрд╛рд╕рд╕реНрдп рдЧреБрдгрдГ ред тАШ рдЕрднреНрдпрд╕реНрддрд╛рдирд╛рдорд╛рджрд┐рдГ’ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджреНрдпреБрджрд╛рддреНрддрддреНрд╡рдореН ред рдХрд╡рд┐рд╢рд╕реНрддрдГ ред рдерд╛рдердШрдЮреНрддрд╛рдгрдГрдЬрдмрд┐рддреНрд░рдХрд╛рдгрд╛рдореН’ рдЗрддреНрдпрдиреНрддреЛрджрд╛рддреНрддрддреНрд╡рдореН ред рдЕрджрдзреБрдГ ред рджрдзрд╛рддреЗрд░реНрд▓рдЩрд┐ рдЭреЗрдГ ‘рд╕рд┐рдЬрднреНрдпрд╕реНрддрд╡рд┐рджрд┐рднреНрдпрд╢реНрдЪ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЬреБрд╕реН ред рдпрджреНрд╡реГрддреНрддрдпреЛрдЧрд╛рджрдирд┐рдШрд╛рддрдГ ред рдЕрдбрд╛рдЧрдорд╕реНрд╡рд░рдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAs soon as born Agni, shines intelligent, swift-moving, skilled in rites, praised by the wise, and liberal in gifts; (and it is he) whom the gods have held as the bearer of oblations at sacrifices, adorable and all-knowing.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

As soon as he is born, Agni shines, becoming ever more visibleтАФhe, the prizewinning horse, the inspired one praised by poets, the one bringing good gifts,
whom the gods have established at the ritesтАФthe one to be summoned, knowing all things, conveying oblations.

Griffith

Agni shines forth when born, observant, mighty, the bountiful, the Singar praised by sages;
Whom, as adorable and knowing all things, Gods set at solemn rites as offeringbearer.

Oldenberg

Agni, when born, shines forth resplendent, the racer, the priest, praised by the sages, the giver of rain, whom the gods placed in the sacrifices, to be magnified, as the omniscient carrier of the sacrificial offerings.

Geldner

Geboren erstrahlt Agni, die Augen auf sich ziehend, der siegreiche, redekundige, von den Sehern gepriesen, gabensch├╢n, den die G├╢tter als berufenen allwissenden Opferfahrer zu den Opfern bestellt haben.

Grassmann

Geboren leuchtet Agni hell erstrahlend, der schnelle, rege, von den S├дngern gepriesene, gabenreiche, der preisenswerthe, allwissende, den die G├╢tter bei den Opferfesten als Ueberbringer der Opfertr├дnke einsetzten.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬOfferer of oblations sit down in your own sphere, for you are cognizant (of holy acts), and station the instrumental tutor of the ceremony in the chief plural ce of the sacred rite; cherisher of the gods, worship the gods, Agni, and bestow abundant food on the founder of the sacrifice.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Yajus. 11.35; in your own sphere: sva u loke: uttaravedy─Бс╕е n─Бbhau, on the centre of the north altar; or, alternatively, sukс╣Ыta yoniс╕е = kс╣Ыс╣гn─Бjine, on the hide of the black antelope; in the chief plural ce of the sacred rite: s─Бday─Б yaj├▒am sukс╣Ыtasya yonau: yaj├▒a = yajam─Бna, yaj├▒asya kart─Бram, who is to be stationed uttame loke, in the best plural ce, or that which enjoys the fruit of the holy rite, sukс╣Ыtajanyopabhogasya sth─Бne

Jamison Brereton

Sit attentive, Hotar, in your own broad place; make the sacrifice sit in the womb of the well-performed (sacrifice).
Pursuing the gods, you will sacrifice to the gods with the offering. Agni, place lofty vigor in the sacrificer.

Griffith

Set thee, O Priest, in, thine own place, observant: lay down the sacrifice in the home of worship.
Thou, dear to Gods, shalt serve them with oblation: Agni, give long life to the sacrificer.

Oldenberg

Sit down, O Hotri, in the space which is thine, as the knowing one. Place the sacrifice in the abode of good works (i. e. on the altar). Eagerly longing for the gods thou shalt worship the gods by offerings. Agni, bestow mighty vigour on the sacrificer.

Grassmann

Priester, sitze achtsam an deinem Orte, setze das Opfer hin in den Schooss des frommen Werkes, g├╢tterspeisend opfere den G├╢ttern mit Trank, gib dem Opfernden grosse Lebenskraft.

English translation:

тАЬProduce, friends, smoke, the showerer (of benefits); indefatigable person st in the contest with (Agni); the heroic Agni is able to encounter hosts, and by him the gods overcome their foes.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Produce smoke: kс╣Ыс╣Зota dh┼лmam, produce fire,by metonymy

Jamison Brereton

Companions, create the smoky bull and without faltering go toward victoryтАЩs prize.
Here is Agni, overwhelming in battles and rich in good heroes, by whom the gods overwhelmed the Dasyus.

Griffith

Raise ye a mighty smoke, my fellow-workers! Ye shall attain to wealth without obstruction.
This Agni is the battle-winning Hero by whom the Gods have overcome the Dasyus.

Oldenberg

Produce a mighty 1 smoke, ye friends. Without fail go forward towards strength. This Agni is the conqueror in battles, rich in valiant men, he by whom the gods have overpowered the Dasyus.

Geldner

Macht riesigen Rauch, ihr Freunde! Ohne Unfall gelangt zum Ziel! Dies ist der Agni, der Schlachtensieger, der Meister, durch den die G├╢tter die Dasyu┬┤s ├╝berw├дltigten.

Grassmann

Lasst Rauch entstehn, o Freunde, geht den Stier um Lab- sal an, nimmer falsch verfahrend; dieser Agni ist ein sehr mann- hafter Feindbesieger, durch den die G├╢tter die D├дmonen besiegt haben.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬThis in every season, Agni, is your plural ce, whence, as soon as genitive rated, you have ever shone; knowing that to be so, Agni, there abide, and thrive by our praises.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Yajurveda 3.14; your plural ce: the allusion is to the araс╣Зi, the stick of vetasa of a┼Ыvattha, or other trees; alternatively, may refer to g─Бrhapatya or household fire; vardhay─Б giraс╕е = give us increase of riches

Jamison Brereton

Here is your womb at its season, from which you shone at birth. Recognizing it, Agni, take your seat here, and then make our songs strong.

Griffith

This is thine ordered place of birth whence sprung to life thou shonest forth.
Knowing this, Agni, sit thee down, and prosper thou the songs we sing.

Oldenberg

This is thy birth-place in due time whence born thou shonest forth; knowing it, O Agni, sit down on it, and make our prayers prosper.

Geldner

Dies ist dein zeitgem├д├Яer Scho├Я, aus dem geboren du erstrahltest. Ihn kennend setz dich nieder, Agni, und f├╢rdere unsere Lobrede!

Grassmann

Hier ist dein angemessner Schooss, aue dem geboren du erstrahltest, ihn kennend, Agni, setze dich hin und segne unsre Lieder.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬWhen (existing) as an embryo (in the wood), Agni is called Tanunap─Бt; when he is genitive rated (he is called) the asura-destroying nar─Б┼Ыam,sa; when he has displayed (his energy) in the material firmament, M─Бtari┼Ыvan; and the creation of the wind is in his rapid motion.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Tan┼лnap─Бt = he who does not consume the person ns of the worshippers, yaс╣гс╣нс╣Ыn─Бm tan┼лс╕е, ┼Ыar─лr─Бс╣Зi nu p─Бtayati, na dahati; or, it may refer to the grandson of the waters;

M─Бtari┼Ыvan = who breathes, ┼Ыvasiti, in the material atmosphere m─Бtari

He is called Tan┼лnap─Бt as the embryo belonging to the lord [=the upper churning stick?]. He becomes Nar─Б┼Ыaс╣Гsa when he is born,
and M─Бtari┼Ыvan when he has assumed his measure in his mother. He became the rush of the wind in leaping forth.

As Germ Celestial he is called Tanunapat, and Narasamsa born diffused in varied shape.
Formed in his Mother he is Matarisvan; he hath, in his course, become the rapid flight of wind.

English translation:

тАЬAgni, who is pronounced by reverential attrition, and deposited with reverential care, and who are far-seeing, render our rites (exempt from defects), and worship the gods (on behalf) of the devout worshipper.тАЭ

The poet is churned out by skillful churning and installed with skillful installation.
O Agni, perform good rites. Sacrifice to the gods for him seeking the gods.

With strong attrition rubbed to life, laid down with careful hand, a Sage,
Agni, make sacrifices good, and for the pious bring the Gods.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMortals have begotten the immortals, the undecaying (Agni), the devourer of oblations, the conveyance (by which they cross over sin), the ten sister fingers intertwined proclaim him born as if it was a male (infant).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Proclaim him born: when the priests and assistants behold the flame break forth, they clap their hands and make sounds of rejoicing, like the parents of a new-born son

Jamison Brereton

Mortals have begotten the immortal one, who is no miscarriage, overwhelming, hard-jawed.
Joined together, ten unwed sisters [=fingers] embrace the male just born.

Griffith

Mortals have brought to life the God Immortal, the Conqueror with mighty jaws, unfailing.
The sisters ten, unwedded and united, together grasp the Babe, the new-born Infant.

Oldenberg

The mortals have generated the immortal one, the тАж 1, advancing one with strong jaws. The ten unwedded sisters 2 united take care of the man (Agni) when he has been born.

Geldner

Die Sterblichen haben den Unsterblichen erzeugt, der keine Fehlgeburt ist, den sich durchsetzenden mit starkem Gebi├Я. Zehn unverm├дhlte Schwestern halten vereint den neugeborenen Mann umfa├Яt.

Grassmann

Die Sterblichen erzeugten den Unsterblichen, der. nimmer fehlgeht, der vorw├дrtsdringt mit festem Gebiss, die zehn vereinten unverm├дhlten Schwestern [die Finger] ergreifen den neugeborenen J├╝ngling.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAgni, who has seven ministering priests, shines eternally; when he has blazed upon the bosom and lap of his mother (earth), he is vociferous (with delight); day by day he never slumbers after he is born from the interior of the (spark) emitting wood.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

From of old, bringing the seven Hotars, he has shone forth in the lap of his mother when he blazed upon her udder.
Day after day, greatly delighting, he does not blink after he has been born from the belly of the lord.

Griffith

Served by the seven priests, he shone forth from ancient time, when in his Mother’s bosom, in her lap, he glowed.
Giving delight each day he closeth not his eye, since from the Asura’s body hewas brought to life.

Oldenberg

He the god of the seven Hotris shone forth from of old, when he flamed up in his mother’s lap, at her udder. Day by day the joyous one never closes his eyes, when he has been born from the Asura’s (i. e. of the Heaven’s?) belly 1.

Geldner

Von sieben Opferpriestern umgeben erstrahlte er seit alters, wenn er im Scho├Яe der Mutter, an ihrem Euter ergl├╝hte. Nicht schlie├Яt der Erfreuliche Tag f├╝r Tag die Augen, nachdem er aus dem Leibe des Asura geboren wurde.

Grassmann

Von Alters her erstrahlte der von sieben Priestern be- diente, als er gl├дnzte au der Mutter Schooss und Euter, nicht nickt er ein der Tag f├╝r Tag erfreuende, seit er erzeugt ward aus dem Leib des Himmlischen.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЕрдорд┐рддреНрд░рд╛рдпреБрдзрдГ) рдЕрдорд┐рддреНрд░реЗрд╖реБ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрд╖реБ рдкреНрд░рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрддрд╛рдиреНрдпрд╛рдпреБрдзрд╛рдирд┐ рдпреИрд╕реНрддреЗ (рдорд░реБрддрд╛рдорд┐рд╡) рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдгрд╛рдорд┐рд╡ (рдкреНрд░рдпрд╛рдГ) рдпреЗ рд╕рджреНрдпрдГ рдкреНрд░рдпрд╛рдиреНрддрд┐ рддреЗ (рдкреНрд░рдердордЬрд╛рдГ) рдкреНрд░рдердорд╛рддреНрдХрд╛рд░рдгрд╛рдЬреНрдЬрд╛рддрдГ (рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордгрдГ) рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдордирдГ (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рдореН) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдВ рдЬрдЧрддреН (рдЗрддреН) рдПрд╡ (рд╡рд┐рджреБрдГ) (рджреНрдпреБрдореНрдирд╡рддреН) рдкреНрд░рд╢рд╕реНрддрдХреАрд░реНрддреНрддрд┐рдорддреН (рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо) рдмреГрд╣рджреНрдзрдирдореН (рдХреБрд╢рд┐рдХрд╛рд╕рдГ) рдЙрддреНрдХрд░реНрд╖рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд╛рдГ (рдЖ) (рдИрд░рд┐рд░реЗ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ (рдПрдХрдПрдХрдГ) рдЬрдирдГ (рджрдореЗ) рдЧреГрд╣реЗ (рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдореН) (рд╕рдореН) (рдИрдзрд┐рд░реЗ) рдкреНрд░рджреАрдкрдпреЗрдпреБрдГ реерезрелрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рдХрд▓реНрдкреЗрди рдЗрдбрд╛рдЧрдордГ ред рддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН ’ рдгреЗрд░рдирд┐рдЯрд┐ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдгрд┐рд▓реЛрдкрдГ ред рдирд┐рдШрд╛рддрдГ ред Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAgni, offerer of oblations, cognizant of rites, inasmuch as we have recourse to you today in this progressing sacrifice, therefore do you steadily convey (the offering to the gods), or tranquilly be at rest, and knowing (the purport of our acts), and wise (in all respects), approach (and accept) the Soma.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Since we chose you here today while the sacrifice was proceeding, o attentive HotarтАФ
you have steadfastly journeyed and you have steadfastly laboredтАФas the knowing one recognizing this, journey here to the soma.

Griffith

As we, O Priest observant, have elected thee this day, what time the solemn sacrifice began,
So surely hast thou worshipped, surely hast thou toiled: come thou unto the Soma, wise and knowing all.

Oldenberg

After we had chosen thee here to-day, O wise Hotri, while this sacrifice was going on, thou hast firmly sacrificed and firmly laboured. Come to this Soma, expert and knowing!

Da wir dich heute bei diesem beginnenden Opfer, du kundiger Hotri, hier erw├дhnt haben - du hast bisher best├дndig geopfert und best├дndig den Dienst versehen - so komm des Weges kundig als Kenner her zum Soma!

Grassmann

Als wir heute dich im Beginne dieses Opfers, o acht- samer Pi’iester, uns hier erw├дhlt hatten, so kamst du auch treu, und treu hast du gewirkt; des Weges kundig, wissend komm zum Soma.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдЪрд┐рдХрд┐рддреНрд╡реЛ рд╣реЛрддреЛ рдпрджреНрдпреЗ рд╡рдпрдорджреНрдпрд╛рд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрдкреНрд░рдпрддрд┐ рдпрдЬреНрдЮреЗ рдпрдВ рддреНрд╡рд╛рд╜рд╡реГрдгреАрдорд╣рд┐ рд╕ рддреНрд╡рдорд┐рд╣ рдзреНрд░реБрд╡рдорд╢рдорд┐рд╖реНрдард╛ рдЙрддрд╛рд╜рдкрд┐ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдирдиреН рдзреНрд░реБрд╡рдордпрд╛рдГ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдБрддреНрд╕рдВрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рд╕реЛрдордореБрдкрдпрд╛рд╣рд┐ реерезремрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЕрде рдХреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рдирд┐рд╢реНрдЪрд▓рдореИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреЗ рдЬрд╛рдпрдд рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдпрддреН) рдпреЗ (рдЕрджреНрдп) рдЗрджрд╛рдиреАрдореН (рддреНрд╡рд╛) рддреНрд╡рд╛рдореН (рдкреНрд░рдпрддрд┐) рдкреНрд░рдпрддреНрдирд╕рд╛рдзреНрдпреЗ (рдпрдЬреНрдЮреЗ) рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрдиреНрддрд╡реНрдпреЗ рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░реЗ (рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН) (рд╣реЛрддрдГ) рд╕рд╛рдзрдиреЛрдкрд╕рд╛рдзрдирд╛рдирд╛рдорд╛рджрд╛рддрдГ (рдЪрд┐рдХрд┐рддреНрд╡рдГ) рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╡рдиреН (рдЕрд╡реГрдгреАрдорд╣рд┐) рд╡реГрдгреБрдпрд╛рдо (рдЗрд╣) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрд╕рдВрд╕рд╛рд░реЗ (рдзреНрд░реБрд╡рдореН) рдирд┐рд╢реНрдЪрд▓рдореН (рдЕрдпрд╛рдГ) рдпрдЬреЗрдГред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд▓рдЩреНрдордзреНрдпрдореИрдХрд╡рдЪрдиреЗ рд╢рдкреЛ рд▓реБрдХреН рд╢реНрд╡реЗрддрд╡рд╛рд╣рд╛рджрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛рддреНрдкрджрд╛рдиреНрддреЗ рдбрд╕реНред (рдзреНрд░реБрд╡рдореН) (рдЙрдд) рдЕрдкрд┐ (рдЕрд╢рдорд┐рд╖реНрдард╛рдГ) рд╢рдордпреЗрдГ (рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдирдиреН) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН (рдЙрдк) (рдпрд╛рд╣рд┐) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрд╣рд┐ (рд╕реЛрдордореН) рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпрдореН реерезремрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ
